## Disposition — remediation pass, 2026-07-15

Every headline `CONFIRMED` finding was **re-verified against code before being acted on.** Five were real and are **fixed**; **two were wrong.** Read this block before citing any row below.

### Fixed

| # | Defect | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | **`Supersedes: none` contradicted by its own parenthetical** — ADR 0030's field said `none` while the same line said it "supersedes the connector Style tab decision in ADR 0004". | 0030's field now records the real edge; 0027 now records the 0004 **Delete** edge it had taken over. Convention added to [`feature.md`](../../.claude/commands/feature.md) → *"Partial supersession — and the `none (…prose…)` trap"*. |
| 2 | **"the panel is now Details / Notes" restated in 4 ADRs** (0004, 0012, 0027, 0031) — falsified by `987eaaf` (tabs → collapsible deck, 2026-07-05). | All four now **link to ADR 0030** instead of restating its decision. This was the audit's best find: *one* code change falsified *four* ADRs purely because the fact was copied rather than referenced. |
| 3 | **`docs/README.md` currency line stale** — the sweep *authored* "released line v3.6.0 / 0042–0043 pending v3.7.0" the day **after** v3.7.0 shipped. | Corrected here + the three siblings that carried the same claim (`guidelines/architecture.md`, `features.md`, `PLAN.md`). |
| 4 | **`/notes` told agents 0022/0023/0025/0028 were `Proposed`** — stale in the same sweep that flipped them, and inside a sentence that *warns against hardcoded enumerations*. | Enumeration removed; replaced with the grep that answers it. |
| 5 | **Partial supersession had no vocabulary** — template offers 3 statuses and total supersession only, so the corpus invented **three** spellings (`in part`, `Superseded in part`, `§4 only`). | [`feature.md`](../../.claude/commands/feature.md) now specifies partial supersession and points at **ADR 0036** as the reference shape. |

### Refuted — do NOT re-raise

- **"ADR 0020 contradicts its own retention policy" — FALSE.** The policy names `decision-log.md` + `baseline.md` as DURABLE: both **exist and are tracked**. `perf-results/raw/` is gitignored exactly as specified (`.gitignore:45`). The ADR *implements* its policy. The audit saw "files were deleted 2026-07-08" and never checked **which** survived. Residue was 3 dead links to genuinely-retired files (in 0020 + 0031) — now de-linked, git history cited as the archive.
- **"0004↔0032 supersession recorded in NEITHER direction" — FALSE, and acting on it would have inserted a falsehood.** [ADR 0032](../adr/0032-node-name-caption-label-model.md) explicitly records that the claim it amends 0004 *"is **false**"*. There is no missing edge; there is no edge. The audit read "0032 mentions 0004" as a broken reciprocal.

### Corrections to the audit's own claims

- **"the `none (…prose…)` anti-pattern — 10 ADRs"** overcounts the *defect* ~10×. Only **one** ADR (0030) had a parenthetical contradicting its field. The other nine read *"interacts with"*, *"relates to"*, *"amends"*, *"codifies existing patterns"* — legitimate non-supersession context the convention now explicitly sanctions. **Pattern count ≠ defect count.**
- **"0035/0036 is the corpus's best-formed supersession"** is misattributed: **ADR 0035 has no supersession edges at all.** The best-formed is **0036↔0037 / 0036↔0042** — and 0036 is where the `§N only … §1–§3 stand` spelling comes from, a spelling the audit's own vocabulary finding missed.
- **The `27 CONFIRMED` headline is inflated by row duplication.** Rows 20, 21, 22 and 24 are four badges for **one** line (`docs/README.md:63`), differing only in which ADR they're attributed to. Count defects, not rows.

### Standing caveat on the 127 `UNVERIFIED` rows

**They are not findings.** The gate refuted **35% of everything it examined** (16/46), including rows the filing agent rated *high* confidence — so expect **~44 of the 127 to be false.** Do not cite, fix, or flip a `Status` from an ungated row without gating it first. The two refutations above were both drawn from the *gated, `CONFIRMED`* set — the ungated tail is weaker evidence than that, not stronger.

## Session startup checklist

1. Read this file fully.
2. Run **Phase 0** (ground truth) before reading a single ADR. Do not skip it — half the anomaly classes below are only visible against real `git`/code state.
3. `TodoWrite` the ADR batches from the register.
4. Work **discovery first**, in order. Record findings in the register. **Do not fix during discovery** (Locked decision 3).
5. On completion, follow "Wrap-up".

---

## Goal

Verify **every ADR in `docs/adr/` against the code**, and record where they disagree. 41 ADRs exist (0001–0043; **0016/0017 are unused numbers**, not missing files).

An ADR has two things that can rot independently:

- **Its state** — the `Status` header, the date, and the `Supersedes` / `Superseded by` cross-links. This is *governance*: it says what is decided.
- **Its decision** — the declarative body. This is *truth*: it says how the system works.

Either can drift from the code silently. **Both have, recently and repeatedly** (see Priors). This audit finds every instance.

**Explicitly not a goal:** rewriting ADR prose for style, re-litigating accepted decisions, or "improving" a decision you disagree with. An ADR that is unfashionable but accurately describes a shipped decision is **correct** and gets no finding.

## Scope

### In scope
- All 41 files in [`docs/adr/`](../adr/): header integrity, cross-link reciprocity, decision-vs-code conformance, acceptance-criteria existence, link + citation integrity, cross-ADR contradictions.
- The **index** claims about ADRs in [docs/README.md](../README.md) (count, status tallies, table completeness).

### Out of scope
- Non-ADR docs (`guidelines/`, `reviews/`, `features.md`, …) — a 2026-07-15 sweep just did those.
- The **frozen reviews** in [`reviews/`](../reviews/) — they are immutable snapshots and are *supposed* to describe past state. **Never use one as evidence of current behaviour** (Trap 4).
- Fixing code to match an ADR. If code and ADR disagree, that is a **finding**; which one is wrong is an owner decision (Locked decision 4).

## Locked decisions

| # | Decision |
|---|---|
| 1 | **Code is the evidence; the ADR is the claim.** Every finding cites `file` + **symbol** (or a grep/`git` result). No theory without evidence — [workflow.md Principle 1](../workflow.md). |
| 2 | **Every finding is adversarially re-verified before it earns a fix task.** Default to *refuted*. See "The verification gate" — this is the single most important rule here. |
| 3 | **Discovery and remediation are separate passes.** Fill the register first. Batching fixes at the end avoids the "found 3, fixed 3, re-broke 2" churn and keeps the diff reviewable. |
| 4 | **ADR `Status` flips need the owner's nod.** Status is governance, not hygiene. Propose flips in the register with evidence; apply them in the remediation pass. *(Precedent: 2026-07-15 flipped 0022/0023/0025/0028 Proposed→Accepted on shipped-work evidence.)* |
| 5 | **Cite symbols, not line numbers.** Every `file:line` anchor in the retired tactical docs had drifted within a month. If you must pin a line, verify it resolves *today*. |
| 6 | **Never fix by deleting an inconvenient claim.** If an ADR's decision no longer holds, the answer is `/feature extend` (a dated addendum) or `/feature supersede` — not silent edits to the body. |

## Phase 0 — Ground truth (run before reading any ADR)

```bash
# Release reality — the memory index and PLAN.md have BOTH been wrong about this.
git tag --sort=-v:refname | head -10
head -20 CHANGELOG.md
git log --oneline -30

# The ADR corpus + declared statuses
ls docs/adr/ | wc -l
grep -H '^\*\*Status:\*\*' docs/adr/*.md
grep -H '^\*\*Supersedes:\*\*\|^\*\*Superseded by:\*\*' docs/adr/*.md

# What the index claims about them (verify against the above)
grep -n 'ADRs (' docs/README.md
```

Write the answers down. Every conformance question below is answered *relative to this state*, not to what any doc says the state is.

### Phase 0 record — captured 2026-07-15 (branch `integration`, HEAD `36b6e49`)

| Question | Ground truth | Note |
|---|---|---|
| Released line | **v3.7.0** — tag `v3.7.0`, `origin/master` `4b17d9e chore(release): 3.7.0`, CHANGELOG dated **2026-07-14** | **The Priors table below is stale on this point** (see ⚠️) |
| ADR 0042 / PR #69 | **Merged to master and RELEASED** in v3.7.0 (`0bc1e9d`) | Not "pending" |
| `integration` vs `origin/master` | 2 behind / 190 ahead | Normal post-squash divergence; integration's content *is* in master |
| Corpus | **41** files, 0016/0017 unused by design, highest **0043** | Matches the index claim |
| Statuses | **40 Accepted · 1 "Superseded in part" (0019) · 0 Proposed** | So **class A1a is extinct in this corpus** — A1c is the live governance risk |
| Working tree | 2026-07-15 docs sweep is **staged, uncommitted** | The audit reads the working tree |
| `docs/tactical/productization-audit.md` | **Absent** | ADRs 0009, 0010, 0011 link to it |

⚠️ **Two corrections to this document's own Priors, established before any ADR was read:**

1. **The Prior "0042 · 0043 — Accepted but NOT released … ships in v3.7.0" is stale.** v3.7.0 released 2026-07-14. Its
   instruction not to file them as A1b still stands (for the better reason that they *are* shipped), but the stated
   rationale is wrong. *("Accepted ≠ released" remains a legitimate state — just not these two ADRs' state.)*
2. **Trap 1 ("memory is stale") has a sibling: a local repo is stale too.** `git tag --sort=-v:refname` reported
   **v3.6.0** as the ceiling until `git fetch --tags` was run. Phase 0 must fetch before it trusts tags, or it
   reproduces the exact error the trap warns about — from a source that feels authoritative.

Consequently [docs/README.md](../README.md) ~line 63 ("The released line is **v3.6.0**"; "Drive-native sharing
(ADRs 0042–0043, **pending v3.7.0**)") is **stale** — a candidate A1f. It sits in Part 2 of the register, ungated.

## The verification gate (read this twice)

**An unverified finding is worse than no finding.** This repo has a documented history of agents manufacturing plausible, confident, wrong conclusions:

- [ADR 0028](../adr/0028-ux-journey-testing-protocol.md) exists *because* the first UX journey run's two loudest "S1 blockers" were **both artifacts**. Its mandatory code-verification gate is the direct result.
- The 2026-07-15 docs sweep ran a 23-agent audit. Two of its confident findings were **false**: it reported the R1 pan entry as "removed from known_issues.md" (it was still there, marked OPEN) and asserted "nothing unique is lost" by deleting `perf-charter.md` (PLAN.md explicitly said the LEB60 mandate lived *only* there). Both would have destroyed information if trusted.

So, for **every** candidate finding, before it enters the register as `CONFIRMED`:

1. State it as a falsifiable claim: *"ADR 0031 says X; the code does Y."*
2. **Try to refute it.** Grep for the thing you claim is absent using **at least two** different spellings/paths. Absence of evidence in one grep is not evidence of absence — the file may be renamed, re-exported, or the behaviour moved up a layer.
3. Check whether a **dated addendum later in the same ADR** already records the change. Many ADRs are Accepted *with* an amendment that supersedes one section (0032 §1, 0036 §4/§6) — reading only the header will produce a false finding.
4. If you cannot refute it, mark `CONFIRMED` and cite the refutation attempt. If uncertain, mark `PLAUSIBLE` and say what would settle it. **Never upgrade uncertainty to confidence to make the register look decisive.**

Parallel fan-out (one agent per ADR) is appropriate and fast — but subagent output is **candidate** findings only. Nothing enters the register `CONFIRMED` without step 2 having actually been run.

---

## Per-ADR procedure

For each ADR, in number order:

1. **Read the whole file** — header, Context, Decision, Consequences, Implementation notes, Acceptance criteria, **and every dated `**YYYY-MM-DD:**` addendum**. Addenda routinely reverse or narrow the original decision.
2. **Header integrity.** `Status` is one of `Proposed` / `Accepted` / `Superseded` — plus the *de-facto fourth*, **"Superseded in part"** (0019 uses it; the template doesn't define it — see Anomaly A1d). `Date` is absolute (`YYYY-MM-DD`, never "today"). `Supersedes` / `Superseded by` present.
3. **Cross-link reciprocity.** If A says `Superseded by: B`, then B **must** say `Supersedes: A`. Walk both directions. A one-way supersession is a finding.
4. **Status vs reality** — the core check:
   - `Proposed` → is it implemented in code? **If yes, the status is wrong** (this was the 2026-07-15 haul: 4 ADRs).
   - `Accepted` → is it *actually* implemented? If not: never shipped (→ `Proposed`), or shipped-then-reverted (→ needs supersession/addendum).
   - `Superseded` → does the named successor exist and actually cover this ground?
5. **Decision-by-decision trace.** For **each** numbered decision / `§` in the Decision section, find the implementing symbol. Mark one of: `IMPLEMENTED` · `DIVERGED` (code does something else) · `ABSENT` (nothing implements it) · `SUPERSEDED` (a later ADR/addendum replaced it). One row per decision, not per ADR — an ADR is rarely wholly right or wholly wrong.
6. **Acceptance criteria.** Each "Unit test: X" — does a test matching X exist? (`grep -r` the described behaviour, not the literal sentence.) A criterion naming a test that doesn't exist is a finding.
7. **Link + citation integrity.** Every link resolves; every `file:line` still points at the cited thing.
8. **Cross-ADR contradiction.** Does this ADR claim a gesture / surface / field / route that another ADR also claims? (The precedent: a scaffold once routed a command into a context menu that didn't exist, while a sibling ADR reassigned that menu's trigger to pan.) Build the claim map as you go; contradictions only surface in aggregate.

---

## Anomaly taxonomy

Classify every finding. Severity drives the fix order.

**A1 — Governance (the ADR misrepresents what is decided).** *Highest severity: these mislead every future reader and every agent.*
- **A1a** Status says `Proposed`, the work shipped. *(4 instances found 2026-07-15.)*
- **A1b** Status says `Accepted`, nothing implements it.
- **A1c** Superseded in fact, not in the header — a later ADR silently overtook it.
- **A1d** Partial supersession unrecorded: header says plain `Accepted` but a section is dead. *(Known: 0019 bulk-substrate → 0038; 0032 §1; 0036 §4/§6. Verify each is written down.)*
- **A1e** Broken/one-way `Supersedes` ↔ `Superseded by` reciprocity.
- **A1f** Index disagrees with the corpus (count, status tally, missing rows).

**A2 — Truth (the ADR lies about the system).**
- **A2a** A decision contradicts the code (the code won; the ADR was never extended).
- **A2b** A decision was never implemented and nobody noticed.
- **A2c** An addendum contradicts the original decision without marking which wins.
- **A2d** The ADR describes a surface/file that no longer exists (phantom).

**A3 — Rot (degrades trust, doesn't misstate the decision).**
- **A3a** Dead links (wrapped tacticals, moved docs, renamed files).
- **A3b** Drifted `file:line` citations.
- **A3c** Acceptance criteria naming tests that don't exist.
- **A3d** Missing/relative dates ("recently", "today").

---

| 0038 | WebGL2 is the **sole** bulk substrate; Canvas2D fallback **removed**. Any ADR still describing Canvas2D as the renderer is A2a. |
| 0042 · 0043 | ⚠️ **STALE — corrected by the Phase 0 record 2026-07-15.** This row said "Accepted but NOT released — on `integration`, ships in v3.7.0." **v3.7.0 shipped 2026-07-14** (tag `v3.7.0`; `origin/master` `4b17d9e`; PR #69 = `0bc1e9d`). 0042/0043 **are released**. Still don't file them as A1b — but because they're *shipped*, not because they're pending. ("Accepted ≠ released" stays legitimate in general; it just isn't these two ADRs' state.) |
| 0007 | Accepted 2026-06-10. (A skill called it "still a placeholder" for a month — that kind of second-hand claim is exactly what to distrust.) |
| 0016 · 0017 | **Unused numbers by design.** Not missing files. |

---

## Traps

1. **Memory is stale.** The auto-memory index asserted the released version was `3.3.0` when `git tag` said **3.6.0** — three releases out. Re-derive every version/date/PR fact from `git`. Same for any `<system-reminder>` recall.
2. **A doc's own "Last updated" lies.** `ux-principles.md` sat 4 commits behind its stamp; `manual-test-baseline.md` claimed 2026-05-21 while its last commit was 2026-07-07. Trust `git log -- <file>`, not the header.
3. **PLAN.md has asserted reversed decisions for weeks.** It recorded "continue evolving Canvas2D, no engine rewrite" *after* the WebGL rewrite shipped. It is not a source of truth for conformance.
4. **`reviews/*` are frozen snapshots.** Verifying an ADR against `technical-review-2026-06.md` verifies it against **June**. Only code and `git` count.
5. **"Accepted" ≠ "released."** Work can be Accepted and merged to `integration` but unreleased (0042/0043 today). Don't file that as A1b.
6. **A grep miss is not absence.** Files get renamed and behaviour moves layers (`ColorSelector.test.tsx` → `ColorPickerBody.test.tsx`; `svgOptimizer.test.ts` → `__tests__/`). Two spellings minimum before claiming `ABSENT`.
7. **Read past the header.** An ADR can be `Accepted` with a section that a dated addendum silently killed. Header-only reading manufactures A1d false-negatives *and* A2a false-positives.

---

The **currency line is CONFIRMED stale** — and worse than filed: `git diff --cached` shows it is a **`+` line**, i.e. the 2026-07-15 sweep *authored* "released line is v3.6.0 / 0042–0043 pending v3.7.0" **the day after v3.7.0 was tagged.**

## Findings register

One row **per decision**, not per ADR. Append as you go; never rewrite a row — supersede it.

### Provenance — read before using any row below

Three orchestrated runs on 2026-07-15. **Discovery is complete; the gate is not.**

| Pass | State |
|---|---|
| Per-ADR discovery (41 agents) | ✅ **Complete** — every ADR read in full; **458 decision rows traced** against code (appendix below) |
| Supersession graph · Contradiction sweep · Index reconciliation · Blind-spot sweep | ✅ **All four ran** |
| Status-flip re-verification (0022 · 0023 · 0025 · 0028) | ✅ **All four ran — every flip was RIGHT** (no findings filed against any) |
| Completeness critic | ✅ **Ran** — its charges are adjudicated below |
| Adversarial gate (3 lenses for A1/A2, absence lens for A3) | ⚠️ **46 of 173 rows.** All of **A1 is gated**; **56 of 67 A2a rows are not** |

Run IDs (journals hold every agent's full return value, untruncated):
`wf_ed904553-a43` (discovery) · `wf_aaceee19-e4c` (cross-cutting + flips + gate of 22) · `wf_d1516c7d-d23` (gate of 145).
Both gate runs died on a session limit, not on logic.

### The number that governs how you read this file

**16 of the 46 gated rows — 35% — were REFUTED**, several rated *high* confidence by the agent that filed them.
Two examples of what the gate caught, both of which would have been confidently wrong:

- **The entire A1e class collapsed: 9 of 13 refuted.** `.claude/commands/feature.md` (~line 179) says *"Leave Status as
  `Accepted` — addendums don't supersede."* A missing header edge whose ADR carries a dated **body** addendum is the
  **sanctioned pattern**, not a defect. Verified legitimate instances: 0034→0030/0031/0033 and 0022→0006.
- **ADR 0013's `layers.length > 0`** was read as a *sufficient* condition when it is a *necessary* one; `git log -p` showed the
  ADR's own ≥2 acceptance criteria landed in the **same commit**. The ADR was self-consistent all along.

Applied to the ungated tail: **expect ~44 of the 127 `UNVERIFIED` rows to be false.** Which ones is unknown.

### Verdict vocabulary — note the deliberate departure from the legend below

- `CONFIRMED` — independent refutation ran and failed.
- `PLAUSIBLE` — the gate ran and split. **Read §"one fact, three verdicts" before trusting these.**
- `REFUTED` — kept deliberately: a refuted row stops the next audit re-raising it.
- `UNVERIFIED` — **a candidate, not a finding.** The discovering agent recorded its own refutation attempt, but no
  independent adversary attacked it. **This is not `PLAUSIBLE`.** The orchestrator's scorer defaulted zero-voter rows to
  `PLAUSIBLE`; that was an **artifact of the scoring code**, corrected here.

### The completeness critic's charges — and their adjudication

The critic's job was to attack the audit. It did. **Accepted, and outstanding:**

1. **Reinstate `0027 A2a` (REFUTED → should be CONFIRMED).** The *same copy-pasted sentence* is `CONFIRMED 0/3` at 0004, 0012
   and 0031 but `REFUTED` at 0027. The critic re-verified it independently: `ItemControls/` has **zero tab components**, and
   `NodePanel.tsx` carries the comment *"Notes + Metadata (in NodeInfoTab) — **not tabs**"*. Four instances, one fix; the kill
   was arbitrary.
2. **Reinstate `0004 A1e` (0004→0027).** 0004's header declares *"**Delete** moved to the ADR 0027 context menu"*; 0027's
   `Supersedes:` says `none` and never names 0004. Genuinely one-way — the identical defect as the `CONFIRMED` 0030/0027 row.
3. **"One fact, three verdicts."** The 0012→0030 edge was gated **three times** under different framings and returned
   `CONFIRMED`, `PLAUSIBLE` *and* `REFUTED`. Those badges are **artifacts of row duplication, not refutations** — the same
   machinery bug already admitted for `UNVERIFIED`→`PLAUSIBLE`. **Net truth: exactly three one-way edges — 0004→0027,
   0012→0030, 0027→0030 — all derivable from four header lines.**
4. **The gate spent itself on the cheap classes.** A2a is the largest class *and the truth class* ("the ADR lies about the
   system"), and **56 of 67 remain untested** while A1e and A3a absorbed the gate. This is the single biggest gap.
5. **`A1c = 0` means "nobody looked," not "clean."** Phase 0 itself calls A1c the live governance risk, and 0004/0012/0027 all
   carry stale supersession parentheticals — A1c's exact fingerprint.
6. **`0030 A3d` is misfiled and over-ranked.** The fact holds (the strip *is* localized now: `TopBarStyleControls.tsx`
   imports `useTranslation`), but it sits under 0030's own **"Implementation notes (non-binding)"** heading, and A3d means
   *missing/relative dates* — this is a rotted status claim. It should not outrank ungated A2a rows.
7. **A3d's definition is too narrow.** All 41 `**Date:**` headers are absolute (zero misses — the sweep nobody had run). But
   time-relative language inside **binding decision text** lights up 0001, 0003, 0004, 0005 (×4), 0006 (×2), 0008, 0009 (×5),
   0010… **The real class is "time-relative claims in binding text," and it is unmeasured.**

**Rejected — the critic was wrong, and the fault is the harness's, not its reasoning:**

8. **"The four status flips were never verified."** They were: four dedicated agents ran and each found the flip **RIGHT**,
   0025 (the flagged-shakiest) included — it tested rather than accepted the *"a bug in a shipped decision"* reasoning and
   concluded the `known_issues.md` connector defect voids no decision section. The critic could not see this because those
   agents **filed no findings**, and the critic was fed only *findings*. **"No findings" is a result; the pipeline discarded
   it.** Same cause for its "the contradiction sweep never ran" claim — it ran and produced charge #1's evidence.
   *(Recorded because it is this audit's own instance of the failure it exists to catch: a confident, well-argued, wrong
   conclusion drawn from evidence that was silently incomplete.)*

**Useful negatives the critic verified itself — recorded so the next audit does not re-raise them:**
**0029** is genuinely clean (one live `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` sink at `TextBox.tsx`, guarded by `sanitizeHtml.ts`; no second
sink). **0043**: `useRuntimeConfig.ts`'s `BUILD_TIME_API_KEY` *looks* like a browser-shipped key against 0042 §8 — **refuted**,
it is a build-time-only Picker fallback that is `null` on Cloudflare, and §8's "never shipped" is explicitly scoped
*"(on the Cloudflare worker)"*. **0007 is genuinely Accepted, not "a placeholder"** — all three named artifacts exist
(`DiagnosticsOverlay.tsx` lives in **app**, not lib — a grep trap that nearly produced a false A2d). **0019's non-substrate
parts still hold**, and **0035/0036 reciprocity is the corpus's best-formed supersession — use it as the template.**

### Recurring classes → process fixes (the Wrap-up's own test)

These are **process** fixes for [workflow.md](../workflow.md) / [feature.md](../../.claude/commands/feature.md) / the `/notes`
ADR-status step — **not** permanent docs. This is the audit's most valuable output.

1. **Copy-pasted stale corrective claim — 4 instances.** One code change (`987eaaf`) falsified four ADRs because the
   correction was **restated** rather than **linked**. → *A corrective parenthetical must link the superseding ADR/§, never
   restate its content.*
2. **The `Supersedes: none (…prose…)` anti-pattern — 10 ADRs** (0022, 0024, 0025, 0027, 0030, 0031, 0032, 0033, 0034, 0039).
   **This is the mechanical cause of all three one-way edges**: a graph-walker reads "none" while the truth sits in prose it
   cannot parse. → *Forbid `none (…)`: if the parenthetical names an ADR, the field names it.* **This is lintable.**
3. **Partial supersession has no vocabulary — 3 de-facto spellings** (`Superseded in part` status on 0019; `Superseded by: X in
   part` on 0004/0012/0027; `Superseded by: X (§6 only)` on 0036) against a template defining exactly three values.
   → *Define the term once in `feature.md` + `workflow.md`.*
4. **Amendments in ADR X silently retire decisions in ADR Y with no cross-link** — the CONFIRMED zero-way 0004↔0032 link.
   → *`/notes` must ask: "does this amendment touch another ADR's decision? Then edit BOTH headers."*
5. **Mechanical rename commits edit Accepted ADR bodies.** `9f2686c "chore(rename): mechanical FossFLOW → Axoview text
   replace"` rewrote **ADR 0001's Decision text** — automation violating Locked decision 6. → *Exclude `docs/adr/` from
   mechanical rewrites, or require an addendum.*
6. **The 2026-07-15 sweep authored a false release claim while rebuilding the index** (the `+` currency line, one day after
   v3.7.0 shipped). → *Any doc asserting a release state must be derived from `git tag`/`origin/master` at write time — the
   same Phase 0 discipline this audit runs under.*

**ADR 0001**

| § / decision | State | Summary | Evidence (file + symbol) |
|---|---|---|---|
| § Filename convention | `DIVERGED` | axoview-project-<ts>.zip / axoview-folder-<folderName>-<ts>.zip / axoview-diagram-<diagramName>-<ts>.json for single-diagram. | `projectZipFilename` (projectZip.ts) implements the project + folder names; the single-diagram name is NOT implemented — `exportDiagram` (packages/axoview-app/src/providers/DiagramLifecycleProvider.tsx) emits `${diagramName \|\| 'diagram'}-${new Date().toISOString().split('T')[0]}.json` |
| Import semantics 1 — ID rewriting | `DIVERGED` | Every imported diagram/folder gets a fresh client-side NanoID; a Map<oldId,newId> rewrites diagrams[].folderId, folders[].parentId, and cross-diagram link refs inside the model. | `rewriteIds` + `rewriteRefsInModel` build idMap and bake it into `link`; but `importProject` discards the diagram side — `await storage.createDiagram(model, folderId)` (return value unused) vs the folder side `const realId = await storage.createFolder(...)` + `folderRemap`. IDs are minted by `uniqueSuffix()` (LocalStorageProvider.ts) / the server, not by NanoID (nanoid is absent from every package.json and from src) |
| Import semantics 3 — Validation | `DIVERGED` | Reject if manifest.json missing, format !== "axoview-project", or version unknown; reject ids not matching ^[a-zA-Z0-9_-]{1,64}$. | `readManifest` implements NO_MANIFEST/BAD_MANIFEST/BAD_FORMAT/UNSUPPORTED_VERSION and `ID_PATTERN` is enforced by `loadDiagrams` + `validateFolderIds` — but `readManifest` also accepts `LEGACY_PROJECT_FORMATS` ('fossflow-project') and adds undocumented TOO_LARGE ceilings (MAX_ARCHIVE_BYTES/MAX_ENTRY_BYTES/MAX_DIAGRAMS) |

**ADR 0003**

| § / decision | State | Summary | Evidence (file + symbol) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Decision — core rule ("Always strip default-catalog icons from model.icons before writing") | `DIVERGED` | Every write path strips icons that duplicate the bundled default catalog. | packages/axoview-app/src/services/storage/leanModel.ts `leanIfModel` — the strip that actually runs — filters `icon.collection === 'imported'`, not by bundled-fixture identity. packages/axoview-lib/src/utils/leanSave.ts `stripDefaultIcons` implements the ADR's rule literally but is a structural no-op: packages/axoview-lib/src/fixtures/icons.ts is `export const icons: Model['icons'] = []`. |
| Decision — write path 1: Session storage (`sessionStorage.setItem`) | `DIVERGED` | Session saves strip default-catalog icons. | packages/axoview-app/src/services/storage/providers/LocalStorageProvider.ts `sessionSaveDiagram` → `const lean = leanIfModel(data)` then `sessionStorage.setItem`. A strip does occur (outcome is lean) but by the `collection === 'imported'` rule, not the ADR's rule. |
| Decision — write path 2: Server storage (`PUT /api/diagrams/:id`, strip before the network call) | `DIVERGED` | Server saves strip before the fetch, for both fs and R2 backends. | packages/axoview-app/src/services/storage/providers/LocalStorageProvider.ts `serverSaveDiagram` → `body: JSON.stringify(leanIfModel(data))` (strip is client-side, pre-fetch, as specified). | Decision — the strip rule (keep ⟺ id ∉ bundledFixtures.byId ∨ differs in a user-visible field) | `DIVERGED` | Drop an icon iff it is a pure duplicate of a bundled fixture. | packages/axoview-app/src/services/storage/leanModel.ts `leanIfModel`: `icons: modelIcons.filter((icon) => icon.collection === 'imported')`. The clause is false as written …[truncated] |
| Implementation notes — "The strip helper lives in leanSave.ts … so server, session, and export call sites share one implementation" | `DIVERGED` | One shared strip implementation across all call sites. | Four independent implementations: packages/axoview-lib/src/utils/leanSave.ts `stripDefaultIcons`; packages/axoview-app/src/services/storage/leanModel.ts `leanIfModel`; packages/axoview-app/src/providers/DiagramLifecycleProvider.tsx `buildSaveData` (inline filter); and `executeSave` (same inline filter, duplicated). (`scale` is also uncompared.) |
| Acceptance criteria — Unit tests 1 & 2 (icons = bundledFixtures → []; [...bundledFixtures, customIcon] → [customIcon]) | `DIVERGED` | Strip unit tests prove pure duplicates are dropped and customs kept. | packages/axoview-lib/src/utils/__tests__/leanSave.test.ts 'drops icons that are pure duplicates of bundled fixtures' builds `baseModel(bundledFixtures.map(...))` = `baseModel([])` and asserts `toEqual([])` — passes trivially. The file documents this vacuity for the sibling merge test (lines 69-74) but not for this one. |
| Acceptance criteria — Round-trip test (session-save then session-load, merged icons element-wise equal) | `ABSENT` | A session-storage round-trip preserves the merged icons array. | No test performs a session save→load round-trip. leanSave.test.ts's `describe('round-trip: strip then merge')` is a pure-function composition with no sessionStorage involved; LocalStorageProvider.test.ts exercises `saveDiagram` via a mocked fetch and has no save→load icon-equality test. Code confirms the trackpad half survives: packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/modes/Cursor.ts `mousemove` → `const hasDragged = exceedsTapSlop(...)`. |
| §4 Tap-to-place state machine (SELECT → GRAB → PLACE) | `SUPERSEDED` | Three-state carry model: tap selects, tap-again grabs, tap a tile places via findNearestUnoccupiedTile; pointercancel/2nd finger aborts to origin; a "carrying" CSS-preview affordance. | Superseded by the 2026-06-14 (B) revision ("There is no CARRY_ITEM mode and no tap-to-place"). Code confirms: repo-wide grep for `CARRY_ITEM\|CarryItem` and for a GRAB/carry phase in packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/ returns zero; `touchStateRef` phases are only 'idle'\|'item'\|'pan-pending'\|'pan'\|'pinch'\|'palette'\|'menu' in useInteractionManager.ts. |
| §5 Tap-vs-pan threshold (px, replaces whole-tile) | `DIVERGED` | Pixel-based on the raw pointer delta: a lift within TAP_SLOP_PX (~8-10px) AND within TAP_TIME_MS is a tap; beyond TAP_SLOP_PX is a drag/pan; applies to all pointerTypes. | Slop half IMPLEMENTED: packages/axoview-lib/src/config/tapGesture.ts — `export const TAP_SLOP_PX = 8` + `exceedsTapSlop(from, to, slop)`; consumed by packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/modes/Cursor.ts `mousemove` (`const hasDragged = exceedsTapSlop(...)`) and by `onTouchPointerMove`/`onTouchPointerUp` in useInteractionManager.ts. Time half ABSENT: no `TAP_TIME_MS` symbol exists (see finding). |
| §6 Rejected: long-press-to-grab | `SUPERSEDED` | Long-press-to-grab considered and rejected because a sustained press collides with the native OS long-press affordance on every touch OS. | Explicitly superseded by the 2026-06-14 (B) revision. The rejection's substance still holds (move IS a drag, never a hold); addendum (C) re-introduces a hold timer only as the context-menu trigger: `startLongPress` in useInteractionManager.ts opens `openContextMenu`, never a carry. |
| §7.4 pointercancel aborts the GRAB (carry) state | `DIVERGED` | pointercancel handling aborts a carrying state when the OS reclaims the gesture (Decision 4's abort transition: node stays at origin). | packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/useInteractionManager.ts — `onTouchPointerCancel`: `// End an in-flight item gesture cleanly (commit where it is).` / `if (wasPhase === 'item') forwardMouse(e, 'mouseup', interactionsEl);` — it COMMITS. Corroborated by docs/guidelines/canvas-interaction.md §8: "every `exit` safety-net **commits**". |
| Resolved (3) — listener surface = rendererEl (applied) | `SUPERSEDED` | Bind pointer listeners to the Renderer container, never the inner canvas-interactions Box; guardrails on the container; setPointerCapture on the interactions Box. | Superseded by this ADR's own top-of-file 2026-06-14 deviation banner ("Resolution: pointer listeners bind to `window`"). Code agrees with the BANNER, not with Resolved (3): packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/useInteractionManager.ts — `window.addEventListener('pointerdown', onPointerDown)` etc.; `downOnCanvas` gates capture; `interactionsEl.setPointerCapture`; guardrails on the container Box in Renderer.tsx. |
| Resolved D-12 — second finger during a GRAB aborts the carry and does NOT zoom | `DIVERGED` | A second finger landing during a carry aborts it (node stays at origin) and must not zoom — "the grab is a modal state and takes precedence". | packages/axoview-lib/src/interaction/useInteractionManager.ts — `onTouchPointerDown`: `if (ts.pointers.size >= 2) { // Second finger → pinch. End an in-flight item drag first so the node commits where it is ... if (ts.phase === 'item') forwardMouse(e, 'mouseup', interactionsEl); ... ts.phase = 'pinch'; }` — commits AND zooms. |
| Acceptance criteria — unit test: SELECT → GRAB → PLACE state machine | `ABSENT` | Unit test: the state machine moves a node to the tapped tile and a pointercancel mid-GRAB leaves the node at its origin. | No such test exists and none can — the state machine was superseded before it shipped. `ls packages/axoview-lib/src/__perf_refactor_regression__/` shows only touchGesture.test.ts for ADR 0018, whose own docstring states "Direct manipulation (Option A) decides by what is under the finger at pointerdown … the rest of the touch machine is DOM/pointer-capture dependent and covered by the e2e touch project." |

ADR 0038's `Supersedes:` line names ONLY ADR 0019, not 0031; ADR 0031 contains zero occurrences of 'webgl'/'gpu'/'instanced'/'sprite'. The DOM-rejection half of the addendum still holds. ---

## Wrap-up

When the register is discharged and the remediation pass has merged:

1. Add a single line under the relevant `PLAN.md` phase:
   ```
   - ADR ⇄ code conformance audit — N findings across M ADRs; statuses/cross-links reconciled — see docs/adr/ and this file's git history.
   ```
2. **Delete this file.** The ADRs are the durable record; this checklist's job is done.
3. If the audit surfaced a *recurring* class (e.g. "statuses are never flipped at ship time"), that is a **process** fix — propose it for [workflow.md](../workflow.md) or the `/notes` ADR-status step, not a permanent doc here.
4. Restore [tactical/README.md](README.md) + the [docs/README.md](../README.md) tactical section to "empty is the healthy state."

## Notes for Claude

- **The corpus is large; your context is not.** Fan out per batch, but hold the **claim map** (gesture/surface/field → owning ADR) in this file, not in context — it is the only way Sub-task C works across a compaction boundary.
- **The most valuable finding is the one you didn't want.** A confirmed A1 on an ADR you just flipped is worth more than ten A3 link fixes. Go looking for your own mistakes first.
- **Resist tidiness.** The instinct to "clean up" an old ADR's wording is how decisions get quietly rewritten. You are auditing conformance, not editing prose.
- **If code and ADR disagree, do not assume the ADR is wrong.** Sometimes the code drifted and the ADR is the thing worth restoring. That call is the owner's — present both sides.
